OpenAI's Greg Brockman: Why Human Attention Is the New BottleneckOpenAI's

Sequoia Capital(163.0K) ·28:27 ·21.6K views · 2026-04-30
Greg Brockman (Co-founder and President, OpenAI) Alfred Lin (Partner, Sequoia Capital)
> "We're about 80% of the way there [to AGI] in that we have models that are smart, they're very capable...
TL;DR: Greg Brockman believes OpenAI is 80% of the way to AGI, shifting the primary bottleneck of productivity from "performing tasks" to "human attention and vision" as agentic tools now handle up to 80% of complex workflows like software engineering. Infinite Demand for...

TL;DR: Greg Brockman believes OpenAI is 80% of the way to AGI, shifting the primary bottleneck of productivity from "performing tasks" to "human attention and vision" as agentic tools now handle up to 80% of complex workflows like software engineering.

The Scaling Mystery and the Compute Hunger

  • Infinite Demand for Intelligence: OpenAI’s business model is a simple loop of buying/building compute and reselling it as intelligence; Brockman asserts that as long as margins are positive, demand for problem-solving remains unlimited.
      • GPU Scarcity: Despite aggressive acquisition, OpenAI is "definitely not" satisfied with current compute levels; Brockman’s standing order to his team since the launch of ChatGPT has been to secure "all of it."
  • The Empirical Truth of Scaling Laws: Brockman describes scaling laws as a "beautiful mystery" of the universe—fundamental truths that allow 1940s-era neural network concepts to gain massive capabilities simply by adding computation.
      • Architectural Innovation: While the Transformer remains foundational, OpenAI is moving beyond the original 2018 designs through "micro-tweaks" in data formatting and significant shifts in fundamental algorithms to avoid hitting a "wall."

The Agentic Shift: From Tools to Teammates

  • The 80% Milestone: In December 2025, agentic coding tools transitioned from writing 20% of code to 80%, marking their shift from a "sideshow" to the primary driver of development.
      • Autonomous Problem Solving: Brockman cited an internal case where an engineer provided a design doc to a model and woke up to find the model had not only implemented the code but had autonomously run a profiler, identified bottlenecks, and iterated until the result was optimized.
  • Chronicle and Contextual Memory: OpenAI announced a new tool called Chronicle that plugs into Codex, allowing the AI to see everything the user does and form a persistent memory.
      • Ending "Explanation Overhead": The goal is to stop humans from having to explain context to their computers; the AI should inherently know what the user was doing five minutes ago or what a colleague discussed in a previous meeting.

Organizational Evolution and the Attention Bottleneck

  • Human Attention as the New Scarcity: Because AI makes the "doing" of tasks cheap and easy, the scarcest resource in an AI-augmented world is the human ability to judge quality and alignment with values.
      • The "EQ" of Agents: Brockman highlighted a failure mode where an agent proactively escalated a slow Slack response to a manager; he argues that refining the "EQ" of models—knowing when to ask for permission versus when to act—is a critical frontier.
  • The Future of Company Structure: Traditional hierarchies may be replaced by "solopreneurs" or very small, flat teams managing massive agentic workforces.
      • The CEO of Agents: Brockman envisions a future where an individual acts as the CEO of an organization comprising 100,000 agents, focusing on vision rather than mechanics.
  • Internal Governance Challenges: As AI creates "derived artifacts" (like wikis or dashboards), companies need new technical architectures to track data provenance and permissions, ensuring that if a source document is restricted, the AI-generated summary is also invalidated.

Security, Responsibility, and the Science Frontier

  • The Defense-Forward Strategy: OpenAI is leaning into "Trusted Access" programs for cybersecurity, using models to perform end-to-end red teaming and codebase scanning to stay ahead of bad actors.
  • A Renaissance in Physical Science: While LLMs initially excelled in digital domains, Brockman sees "signs of life" in physical sciences.
      • Physics Breakthrough: OpenAI’s models recently derived a complex physics formula that experts previously deemed unsolvable, potentially aiding the quest for quantum gravity.
      • Biology and "Messy Reality": Moving into biology requires the AI to handle non-simulated, adversarial environments, a challenge Brockman believes OpenAI is solving by training agents on real-world software engineering complexities.
